    StackExchange.ready(function () {

        var location = 0;
        if ($("body").hasClass("questions-page")) {
            location = 1;;
        } else if ($("body").hasClass("question-page")) {
            location = 1;;
        } else if ($("body").hasClass("faq-page")) {
            location = 5;;
        } else if ($("body").hasClass("home-page")) {
            location = 3;;
        }

        $('#tell-me-more').click(function () {
            StackExchange.using("gps", function () {
                StackExchange.gps.track("hero.action", { hero_action_type: 'cta', location: location }, true);
            });
        });
        $('#herobox #close').click(function () {
            StackExchange.using("gps", function () {
                StackExchange.gps.track("hero.action", { hero_action_type: "minimize", location: location }, true);
            });
            $.cookie("hero", "mini", { path: "/", expires: 365 });
            $.ajax({
                url: "/hero-mini",
                success: function (data) {
                    $("#herobox").fadeOut("fast", function () {
                        $("#herobox").replaceWith(data);
                        $("#herobox-mini").fadeIn("fast");
                    });
                }
            });
            return false;
        });

<td class="postcell">
<div>
    <div class="post-text" itemprop="text">

<p>I'm trying to secure my <code>authorized_keys</code> file to prevent it from being modified. I run this:</p>

<pre><code>[root@localhost]# chattr +i authorized_keys 
chattr: Inappropriate ioctl for device while reading flags on authorized_keys
</code></pre>

<p>I think it may be due to the filesystem:</p>

<pre><code>[root@localhost]# stat -f -c %T /home/user/
nfs
</code></pre>

<p>there is a way to modify it with chattr?</p>
    </div>

<div id="answer-90327" class="answer accepted-answer" data-answerid="90327" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer" itemprop="acceptedAnswer">

            <td class="votecell">
                

<div class="vote">

<td class="answercell">
    <div class="post-text" itemprop="text">
<p>NFS doesn't have a concept of immutable files, which is why you get the error. I'd suggest that you just remove write access from everyone instead, which is probably close enough for your purposes. </p>

<pre><code>$ &gt; foo
$ chmod a-w foo
$ echo bar &gt; foo
bash: foo: Permission denied
</code></pre>

<p>The main differences between removing the write bit for all users instead of using the immutable attribute:</p>

<ul>
<li>The immutable attribute must be unset by root, whereas chmod can be changed by the user owning the file;</li>
<li>The immutable attribute removes the ability to remove the file without removing the immutable attribute, which removing the write bit doesn't do (although you can change the directory permissions to disallow modification, if that is acceptable).</li>
</ul>

<p>If either of these things matter to you when dealing with authorized_keys, you probably have a more fundamental problem with your security model.</p>
    </div>

<td class="answercell">
    <div class="post-text" itemprop="text">
<p>Correct this will not work over NFS.</p>

<p>However, on the server where this directory is exported try run your chattr command.   With a couple of gotchas</p>

<p>You may need to enable ACLs:</p>

<pre><code>$ mount -o remount,acl /
</code></pre>

<p>(To make that change permanent edit your /etc/fstab)</p>

<p>SELinux may get in your way:</p>

<p>To find out for sure:</p>

<pre><code>$ ls -Z
</code></pre>
    </div>

<div id="answer-60718" class="answer accepted-answer" data-answerid="60718" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer" itemprop="acceptedAnswer">

            <td class="votecell">

<td class="answercell">
    <div class="post-text" itemprop="text">
<p>The immutable attribute may be set on the file. Remove it with chattr -i </p>

<td class="answercell">
    <div class="post-text" itemprop="text">
<p>Several solution exists, some among them:</p>

<ul>
<li>you have a filesystem does not lets you eg. uid:gid, eg: FAT</li>
<li>the drive has been mounted read-only</li>
<li>SELinux or other security enforcers apply</li>
<li>filesystem is set to read-only mode (xfs_freeze, for example)</li>
</ul>
    </div>

    <tbody><tr>

<td class="answercell">
    <div class="post-text" itemprop="text">
<p>Try this:</p>

<p>[root@ root]# chattr -ais /bin/ls</p>

<p>after changing the ownership and group back to root. </p>

<td class="answercell">
    <div class="post-text" itemprop="text">
<p>Funny. Did you check the system logs (/var/log/messages, /var/log/syslog, output of dmesg) for any clues?</p>

<p>Possible reasons:</p>

<ul>
<li>You are running some security-enhanced Linux, such as <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Security-Enhanced_Linux" rel="nofollow noreferrer">SELinux</a>. These place restrictions even on what root can do.</li>
<li>The file is on a file system that does not support file ownership, such as (V)FAT. Depending on mount options chmod/chown will give you errors.</li>
</ul>
    </div>
    <table class="fw">
    <tbody><tr>
    <td class="vt">

<div class="vote">
        <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="224383" />
        <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a>

<td class="answercell">
    <div class="post-text" itemprop="text">
<p>I had same problem.</p>

<pre><code>$ chattr -V -i dir
chattr 1.41.12 (17-May-2010)
Flags of dir set as s----a---------
</code></pre>

<p>Which was not enough. So i added the 'sa'</p>

<pre><code>$ chattr -V -ais dir
chattr 1.41.12 (17-May-2010)
Flags of dir set as ---------------
$ chown root dir
$
</code></pre>

<p>Problem solved :)</p>
    </div>

    <tbody><tr>

<div id="answer-60712" class="answer" data-answerid="60712" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer">
    <table>
        <tbody><tr>
            <td class="votecell">
                

<div class="vote">
        <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="60712" />
        <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a>

<td class="answercell">
    <div class="post-text" itemprop="text">
<p>on what kind of Filesystem is the "ps" file you are trying to chown ? Is the fs mounted as ro (readonly) ?</p>

<p>if you are talking about /bin/ps, on debian it's always like:</p>

<pre><code>-rwxr-xr-x 1 root root 76132 2009-05-28 10:48 /bin/ps*
</code></pre>
    </div>

            <div style="display: block;" class="comment-body">
                <span class="comment-copy">If your system was hacked, then you don't want to put files back. You have <i>no</i> way of telling what's been broken, and nothing on the system is trustworthy. Wipe, and reinstall from backups.</span>
                    – <a href="/users/2598/cian" title="5,092 reputation" class="comment-user">Cian</a>
                <span class="comment-date" dir="ltr"><a class="comment-link" href="#comment48541_60712"><span title="2009-08-31 10:07:29Z" class="relativetime-clean">Aug 31 '09 at 10:07</span></a></span>

        </td>
        <td class="comment-text">
            <div style="display: block;" class="comment-body">
                <span class="comment-copy">As Cian said, if your system was hacked and they got root access, don't replace files. It may <i>still</i> contain a (nearly) invisible rootkit that hijacks system calls. It may still be sniffing passwords, it may still have opened backdoors in your services, and and and (infinite number of possible things a hacked machine may contain).  The reasonable thing to do is to turn off the machine and study its contents offline, by putting the disk to another box. Don't trust this machine at all and don't replace any binaries, they may contain valuable information to discover what the rootkit does.</span>
                    – <a href="/users/17698/kargig" title="326 reputation" class="comment-user">kargig</a>
                <span class="comment-date" dir="ltr"><a class="comment-link" href="#comment48564_60712"><span title="2009-08-31 11:38:51Z" class="relativetime-clean">Aug 31 '09 at 11:38</span></a></span>

<div id="answer-60720" class="answer" data-answerid="60720" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Answer">
    <table>
        <tbody><tr>
            <td class="votecell">
                

<div class="vote">
        <input type="hidden" name="_id_" value="60720" />
        <a class="vote-up-off" title="This answer is useful">up vote</a>
        <span itemprop="upvoteCount" class="vote-count-post ">0</span>
        <a class="vote-down-off" title="This answer is not useful">down vote</a>




</div>

            </td>
            


<td class="answercell">
    <div class="post-text" itemprop="text">
<p>Every "guess" made by other answers is possible. A debugging hint may be to do a <strong>strace</strong> of the command, and look into the output in order to see what is the real problem in the syscalls itself.</p>

<pre><code>strace chown root /bin/ps 2&gt;&amp;1 | less 
</code></pre>
    </div>

    <tbody><tr>
